================================================================================
DOMAIN: EPISTEMOLOGY (11 positions)
================================================================================

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-138
Work: Unknown
Title: Counterfactuals as epistemic probability relations

Position:
Counterfactuals don't really say anything about events or anything concrete... Counterfactuals merely register confirmation relations among propositions.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-139
Work: Unknown
Title: Counterfactuals are crypto-probability propositions

Position:
if A had been the case, then B would have been the case means: The proposition K and P(A) gives a high probability to P(B), where K is the conjunction of propositions we know to be true, minus the proposition that A and B were not the case.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-140
Work: Unknown
Title: Probability is epistemic not metaphysical

Position:
It is clear, then, that probability is an epistemic, not a metaphysical, notion. Probability is a logical relation between propositions; it is not a property of states of affairs.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-141
Work: Unknown
Title: False propositions probabilify other propositions

Position:
It must be kept in mind that false propositions probabilify other propositions just like true ones. The proposition the moon is made of cheese is false, but that doesn't stop it from giving a very high degree of probability (essentially 100%) to the proposition there is a piece of cheese that weighs more than 100 lbs.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-142
Work: Unknown
Title: Counterfactual truth independent of empirical discoveries

Position:
surely the truth of (4) is not contingent on the outcome of such inquiries. So the factualist has mis-analyzed (4).

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-143
Work: Unknown
Title: The Frequency Theory of Probability is false

Position:
The Frequency Theory of Probability (FT) tells us that, in W2, the probability of a computer's never malfunctioning is 100%... This is plainly false. In each universe, the likelihood of computer-error is the same, even though, in W1 the likelihood seems high and, in W2, the likelihood seems low. (Chapter 7, 'Statistical trends reflective of, but distinct from, probabilities')

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-155
Work: WORK-043
Source: Chapter 9

Position:
Cartesian Certainty About Current Thought-Contents

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-156
Work: WORK-043
Source: Chapter 9

Position:
Content Externalism Makes Self-Knowledge Impossible

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-157
Work: WORK-043
Source: Chapter 9

Position:
Epistemic Situations Don't Determine Contents Under Externalism

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-158
Work: WORK-043
Source: Chapter 9

Position:
Slow-Switching Arguments Beg the Question

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-159
Work: WORK-043
Source: Chapter 15

Position:
We Can Know Propositions Without Knowing All Constituents


================================================================================
DOMAIN: FREE WILL (10 positions)
================================================================================

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: FW-014
Work: Unknown
Title: Determinism defined as universal causation

Position:
Dr. K: Determinism is the doctrine that nothing is uncaused. MAX: So if determinism is correct, then how the world is now determines exactly how it will be in the future.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: FW-015
Work: Unknown
Title: Indeterminism entails some chaos

Position:
Dr. K: If there is a single uncaused event, then indeterminism is correct, even if the universe is otherwise completely deterministic. And it doesn't matter how minute that event is.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: FW-016
Work: Unknown
Title: Indeterminism threatens freedom more than determinism

Position:
Dr. K: Indeterminism is more of a threat to freedom than determinism. In fact, determinism is not a threat to freedom. It is in fact necessary for it. Determinism is as necessary for freedom as indeterminism is fatal to freedom.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: FW-017
Work: Unknown
Title: External indeterminism doesn't increase freedom

Position:
Dr. K: would we be more free in W than we are here? MAX: No; if anything, less free. At least in our world, there are dependable mechanisms. So we can control it. But in W, we can't even do that.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: FW-018
Work: Unknown
Title: Internal indeterminism doesn't increase freedom

Position:
Dr. K: So to the extent that your nervous system is indeterministic, its condition at time t leaves it open whether I will make the requisite bodily movements... Your berry-knowledge won't necessarily lead to the right decision unless the mechanisms that convert knowledge into intentions are intact.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: FW-019
Work: Unknown
Title: Mechanisms require determinism

Position:
Dr. K: A mechanism is something that can be relied on to produce on output of a certain kind, when given an input of a certain kind... Where there are mechanisms, there is determinism. Where there is indeterminism, there are no mechanisms.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: FW-020
Work: Unknown
Title: Indeterministic minds are incoherent

Position:
Dr. K: The more its future condition fails to cohere with its present condition... it is therefore no mind at all, but rather a series of mutually isolated minds... Since its earlier states fail to cohere with its later states... So it exists only for an instant. And therefore doesn't exist at all.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: FW-021
Work: Unknown
Title: Freedom requires appropriate mental state responsiveness

Position:
Dr. K: So this inner freedom you are discussing---one has it to the extent that one's current mental state embodies the appropriate sort of responsiveness to one's previous mental states... possession of this inner freedom is not about having a mind whose mental states don't determine one another; it is about having a mind whose mental states determine one another in the right way.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: FW-022
Work: Unknown
Title: Freedom as causal integration

Position:
Dr. K: Yes, a person is free if his mind is constitutive of the right sort of causal integration. MAX: And my view is that a person is not free unless his mind is constitutive of the right sort of causal integration, but I don't grant that a person is free if that condition is satisfied.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: FW-023
Work: Unknown
Title: Responsibility requires agent-constitutive causation

Position:
Dr. K: For an action on Stalin's part to be free is for Stalin to be responsible for it. And for Stalin to be responsible for it is for Stalin-constitutive forces to be responsible for it... And until such forces, such Stalin-constitutive forces, are in existence, we cannot talk of Stalin's being made to do this or that.

DOMAIN: LOGIC (16 positions)
================================================================================

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: LOGIC-052
Work: Unknown
Title: Logic as the study of formal truth

Position:
Dr. K: It is the study of formal truth... A formal truth is a statement that holds entirely in virtue of its own structural properties.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: LOGIC-053
Work: Unknown
Title: Mathematical logic studies statement-functions

Position:
Dr. K: Mathematical logic studies statement-functions. Most other branches of mathematics study numerical functions.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: LOGIC-054
Work: Unknown
Title: Negation preserves incompatibility

Position:
Dr. K: The negation of a statement is incompatible with that statement... The negation of someone is tall is it is not the case that someone is tall; in other words, nobody is tall.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: LOGIC-055
Work: Unknown
Title: Truth-functional operators defined by truth tables

Position:
Dr. K: 'and', 'or', and 'not' are very special, since they are truth-functional, meaning that whether or not the output sentence is true depends only on whether or not input sentences are true.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: LOGIC-056
Work: Unknown
Title: Non-truth-functional operators exist

Position:
MAX: Because even if P and Q are both true, 'P because Q' isn't necessarily true... Given only that P is true, it does not follow that 'Jim knows that Mary is in Alaska' is true.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: LOGIC-057
Work: Unknown
Title: Recursive functions define logical systems

Position:
Dr. K: Notice that each of these functions if defined for its own outputs... this means that each of these functions is recursive... a system of logic is a recursively defined statement class. And logic is the study of such classes.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

DOMAIN: METAPHYSICS (8 positions)
================================================================================

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: META-051
Work: Unknown
Title: The universe is counter-entropic through life

Position:
MASTER: TO THE EXTENT THAT THE WORLD FALLS WITHIN THE SCOPE OF THE DISCIPLINE OF PHSYICS, IT IS ENTROPIC... BUT NOTICE THAT, TO THE EXTENT THE WORLD FALLS WITHIN THE SCOPE OF BIOLOGY, IT IS COUNTER-ENTROPIC.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: META-052
Work: Unknown
Title: Indeterminism prevents composite objects

Position:
Dr. K: To the naked eye, a billiard ball looks like a single indivisible object. But it consists of trillions of micro-particles interacting with each one another... if those interactions weren't governed by deterministic laws... each particle would go its own way... and the billiard ball would powder into nothingness.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: META-053
Work: Unknown
Title: States of affairs are causal processes

Position:
It seems to me part of our concept of a state of affairs (leaving aside completely instantaneous ones) that such things are causal sequences.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: META-054
Work: Unknown
Title: Temporal priority defined causally

Position:
A standard definition of temporal priority is this: x precedes y iff some possible causal sequence (e.g., a beam of light) connects x to y... So it seems to me that x precedes y iff there is some causal process starting with x that ends with y.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: META-041
Work: WORK-043
Source: Throughout

Position:
Propositions Exist

================================================================================
DOMAIN: MODAL LOGIC (6 positions)
================================================================================

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: MODAL-025
Work: Unknown
Title: Factualist analysis of counterfactuals fails

Position:
The factualist view is not tenable... Two deterministic worlds cannot differ from each other with respect to a single state of affairs unless they differ with respect to a series of states of affairs extending back into the furthest recesses of time.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: MODAL-026
Work: Unknown
Title: Possible worlds analysis requires circular mixture of determinism

Position:
The factualist needs the world to be simultaneously characterized by different mixtures of determinism and indeterminism. But this is an incoherent requirement.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: MODAL-027
Work: Unknown
Title: Indeterminism destroys counterfactual truth conditions

Position:
if the macro-world here is indeterministic, then the factualist position is quite definitely false... The most one can say is: there is a 54% chance that it starts in w. Really, the proposition in w, under the circumstances described, the car starts seems to lack truth-value.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: MODAL-028
Work: Unknown
Title: Worlds are not sets of propositions

Position:
Our world is not a set of propositions. Our world is something which makes sets of propositions be true or false. Any world deserving of the name is something which makes propositions be true or false. A set of propositions does not make propositions be true or false.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: MODAL-029
Work: Unknown
Title: Weak factualism is incoherent

Position:
the weak-factualist denies that counter-factuals merely register relations of probabilification (or entailment) among propositions. And he denies that counter-factuals register facts relating to other worlds (in any genuine sense of 'world'). So his position is completely incoherent.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: MODAL-030
Work: Unknown
Title: Maximal consistent sets useless for counterfactuals

Position:
alternative worlds, in the sense of maximal consistent sets of propositions, are absolutely useless for analyzing counter-factuals.


================================================================================
DOMAIN: PHILOSOPHY OF ACTION (8 positions)
================================================================================

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: ACTION-008
Work: Unknown
Title: Action requires self-change

Position:
MASTER: NO, IT CANNOT, SINCE TO ACT IS TO CHANGE ONESELF.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: ACTION-009
Work: Unknown
Title: Power presupposes freedom

Position:
Dr. K: There is freedom, and there is power. Power is the ability to convert freedom into desired results. But power presupposes the existence of freedom, and must therefore be distinguished from it.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: ACTION-010
Work: Unknown
Title: Intentions vs desires in action explanation

Position:
Dr. K: Intentions are grounded one's personality. Desires need not be so grounded. There are free floating desires: desires that are in one, but not of one.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: ACTION-011
Work: Unknown
Title: Compulsive actions achieve opposite of conscious intention

Position:
Dr. K: the end-result of a compulsively performed action is the opposite of the consciously intended result---and therefore coincides with the unconsciously intended result... [Compulsive kindness] affects her in the same way as acts of hostility. For that is what they are.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: ACTION-012
Work: Unknown
Title: Authentic action requires alignment of values and desires

Position:
Dr. K: Actual actions must embody beliefs as well as desire. But also necessary that the values in question be in alignment with the desires in question... Desire-driven acts that do not embody values have the authenticity of veritable actions, but not the requisite sublimity, and value-driven acts that do not embody desire have the requisite sublimity of veritable actions... The former are real, but they aren't actions. The latter are actions, but they aren't real.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: ACTION-013
Work: Unknown
Title: Compulsive behavior as leaking not acting

Position:
MAX: even though those actions, for lack of a better word, do discharge Max's hatred of his mother, it isn't Max who is doing the discharging. It is rather that his sadism is leaking out of him... it almost fails to be his behavior. It is almost more appropriate to describe it as behavior that he undergoes than it is to describe it as behavior that he engages in.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: ACTION-014
Work: Unknown
Title: Deracinated values possess the agent

Position:
Dr. K: given how deracinated his values are---how lacking in any instinctual basis---it is less appropriate to describe them as values that he has than it is to describe them as values that have him.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: ACTION-015
Work: Unknown
Title: True agency requires ideals not just passion

Position:
Dr. K: True agency is about the fulfillment of ideals---not necessarily ethical ideals, but ideals of some kind or other---and where there are no values there are ipso facto no ideals... Where there is desire without values, there is passion---in both the contemporary and the etymological senses of the word---but not action.

================================================================================
DOMAIN: PHILOSOPHY OF SCIENCE (9 positions)
================================================================================

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: SCI-047
Work: Unknown
Title: Laws cannot be defined except via counterfactuals

Position:
the possible-worlds analysis of counterfactuals is guilty of covert circularity. For, thus analyzed, counterfactuals can only be understood in terms of laws of nature... But there is widespread agreement that the concept of a law cannot itself be defined except in terms of the notion of a counterfactual (a law is inter alia something that supports counterfactuals).

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: SCI-048
Work: Unknown
Title: Probability definable from actual events only

Position:
I also argue that the relevant kind of probability can be defined wholly in terms of what has happened (not what would happen and not even what must happen in a nomic sense). So my analysis isn't guilty of any kind of circularity.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: SCI-049
Work: Unknown
Title: Critique of Humean analysis of laws

Position:
Hume says that laws are regularities involving certain kinds of states of affairs. But this presupposes that the notion of a state of affairs is a non-causal one. For obviously if states of affairs are themselves causal processes, then Hume's analysis becomes viciously circular.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: SCI-050
Work: Unknown
Title: Probability must be interpreted causally, not statistically

Position:
When it is said that that probability of a computer-malfunction is greater than 0%, the statement being made is to be interpreted causally, not statistically. What is being said is that, the laws of physics being what they are and the construction of the computer being what it is, it is a possibility, albeit one that may never be actualized, that brand-new/well-constructed/etc. computers malfunction. (Chapter 7, Conclusion)

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: SCI-051
Work: Unknown
Title: Statistics are evidence of probabilities but not themselves probabilities

Position:
Statistics are evidence of probabilities; statistics are not themselves probabilities. According to FT [Frequency Theory], statistics are identical with probabilities; therefore, FT is false. Also, statistics are only as truth-conducive as they are consistent with the causal mechanisms that generate them. (Chapter 7, 'Evidence of probabilities vs. actual probabilities')

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: SCI-052
Work: Unknown
Title: The W1/W2 thought experiment refutes the Frequency Theory of Probability

Position:
In W2, the likelihood that a given computer will behave in a program-compliant doesn't exceed the likelihood that a given computer in W1 will do so: the two probabilities coincide. But in W2 the previously-described rash of coincidences obscures the deterministic, and therefore that probabilistic, structure of events. (Chapter 7, 'Probability in relation to higher-order mechanisms')

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: SCI-053
Work: Unknown
Title: Probability remains constant even when statistics are misleading due to coincidence

Position:
In a world governed by the same biological---and non-biological laws as ours, but in which by sheer coincidence smokers never got cancer/emphysema, doctors would be no less wrong than they would in our world to tell their patients that smoking was harmless... the probability, in that world, that a given smoker would succumb to cancer/emphysema would coincide with the corresponding probability in our world. (Chapter 7, 'Evidence of probabilities vs. actual probabilities')

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: SCI-054
Work: Unknown
Title: Worlds with identical laws have identical probabilities regardless of statistical divergences

Position:
In each universe, the likelihood of computer-error is the same, even though, in W1 the likelihood seems high and, in W2, the likelihood seems low... What is going on is that, in W1, the statistics are consistent with the deterministic-probabilistic structure of the operative laws, whereas in W2 they are not. (Chapter 7, 'Statistical trends reflective of, but distinct from, probabilities')

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: SCI-055
Work: Unknown
Title: Worlds with different causal/nomic structures have different probabilities even if event-sequences are identical

Position:
Derived from the W1/W2 argument and the conclusion that 'probability... is to be interpreted causally, not statistically.' If probability depends on causal/nomic structure, then different causal/nomic structures entail different probabilities regardless of event-patterns. This directly refutes epistemic or statistical interpretations of probability.

DOMAIN: PSYCHOLOGY (11 positions)
================================================================================

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: PSY-131
Work: Unknown
Title: Consciousness maximizes energy efficiency

Position:
STUDENT: RIGHT. TO THE EXTENT THAT AN ORGANISM HAS A MENTAL DIMENSION, IT IS MORE ENERGY-EFFICIENT THAN IT WOULD OTHERWISE, PSYCHOLOGICAL GROWTH BEING A PARTICULARLY EXTREME WAY OF INCREASING AN ORGANISM'S LEVEL OF ENERGY-EFFICIENCY.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: PSY-132
Work: Unknown
Title: Obsessive beliefs are pseudo-beliefs

Position:
Dr. K: if someone obsesses about his hatred of so and so, that is because he is not yet done with so and so. He is still attached to that person... if someone obsessionally believes that such and such, it is because what he actually believes is the opposite of such and such.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: PSY-133
Work: Unknown
Title: Compulsive actions are pseudo-actions

Position:
Dr. K: If one compulsively does such and such, it is because one's real intention is to do the opposite of such and such. If a given person compulsively avoids his ex-girlfriend, it is because he wants to see her.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: PSY-134
Work: Unknown
Title: OCD essence is ambivalence

Position:
Dr. K: the essence of OCD is ambivalence. The compulsively doting son both loves and hates his mother. He loves her, and therefore feels obliged to have lunch with her on Sunday. But he also hates her.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: PSY-135
Work: Unknown
Title: Doing and undoing in OCD

Position:
Dr. K: it is because of this emotional polarity within him that the obsessional engages in what Freud refers to as 'doing and undoing.' He does a given thing. Then he undoes it. And then undoes his undoing of it.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: PSY-136
Work: Unknown
Title: OCD behavior as overdetermined

Position:
MAX: So it is 'overdetermined', to use another expression of Freud's. Dr. K: Precisely... And it also has to do with his undischarged libido.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: PSY-137
Work: Unknown
Title: Symbolic representation in OCD symptoms

Position:
Dr. K: The stove represents undischarged libido... What he wants is for the stove to explode. The stove represents his passionate desire for his girlfriend. His 'fear' the stove will explode is really his desire that he---meaning his genital region---will, so to speak, 'explode.'

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: PSY-138
Work: Unknown
Title: Awareness without consciousness in the obsessional

Position:
Dr. K: This young man obviously is not consciously aware of his mother's treachery. But he is aware of it. He probably does not quite see it for what it is, even at the level of unconsciousness. But he is surely aware of it.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: PSY-139
Work: Unknown
Title: Single ultimate determinant despite overdetermination

Position:
MAX: ultimately, his behavior has only determinant, this being his sexual frustration... He is ambivalent towards his mother because she is causing him to be sexually frustrated. So his ambivalence and his sexual frustration are, at least in this context, operating as a single cause. Dr. K: Admirably well put, Max.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: PSY-140
Work: Unknown
Title: Consciousness of hatred eliminates compulsions

Position:
MAX: What happens when it [unconscious hatred] becomes conscious? Dr. K: What happens is that any associated compulsions vanish.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: PSY-141
Work: Unknown
Title: Compulsive time management as defense

Position:
MAX: He may be compulsively on time—hyper on time, as it were—as a way of insulating himself against his wish not to show up at all. Dr. K: Precisely.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: REL-023
Work: Unknown
Title: Omniscience precludes action

Position:
MASTER: NO. ACTION PRESUPPOSES IGNORANCE. IF YOU KNOW WITH CERTAINTY, WHAT IS GOING TO HAPPEN, YOU CANNOT COHERENTLY ATTEMPT TO INFLUENCE WHAT IS GOING TO HAPPEN AND YOU CAN THEREFORE CANNOT INTENT TO ACT.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: REL-024
Work: Unknown
Title: Omnipotence precludes feeling

Position:
MASTER: NO. ONLY A BEING THAT IS CAPABLE OF BEING CHANGED CAN EXPERIENCE FEELINGS. AND IF A BEING IS CAPABLE OF BEING CHANGED, THEN IT IS NOT CAPABLE OF FEELING.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: REL-025
Work: Unknown
Title: Immutability precludes self-change

Position:
MASTER: NO, IT IS NOT. TO BE CHANGE ONESELF IS TO BE CHANGED, ALBEIT BY ONSELF. AND, OBVIOUSLY, A BEING THAT CANNOT BE CHANGED CANNOT BE CHANGED BY ANYTHING, INCLUDING ITSELF.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: REL-026
Work: Unknown
Title: Omnipotence entails impotence

Position:
STUDENT: SO IF A BEING IS ALL-POWERFUL, IT IS COMPLETELY IMPOTENT. MASTER: CORRECT.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: REL-027
Work: Unknown
Title: Traditional divine attributes are incoherent

Position:
MASTER: CORRECT. STUDENT: AND FOR SIMILAR REASONS, WE ARE ALSO TO CONCLUDE THAT THE CONCEPT OF AN ALL-KNOWING BEING IS INCOHERENT.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: REL-028
Work: Unknown
Title: Consciousness is inherent in existence itself

Position:
MASTER: SO YOU SEE, MY SON, IT IS ONLY TO THE EXTENT THAT THE UNIVERSE IS DISINTEGRATING---THAT IT IS CEASING TO BE WHAT IT IS—THAT IT LACKS CONSCIOUSNESS; AND CONTRARIWISE, TO THE EXTENT THAT THE UNIVERSE IS GROWING—THAT IT IS BECOMING WHAT IT TRULY IS---IT HAS CONSCIOUSNESS.

ID: ACTION-006
Work: Unknown
Title: Compatibilism About Free Will

Position:
Free will is compatible with determinism. One acts freely when actions result from one's own desires and deliberations. **EPISTEMOLOGY (15 positions): EP-001 to EP-026**

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: ACTION-001
Work: Unknown
Title: Intentions as System-Level Judgments

Position:
Intentions = judgments about how to consolidate psychological architecture. NOT desires.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: ACTION-002
Work: Unknown
Title: Values Distinct from Desires

Position:
Values = beliefs about what consolidates psychological architecture. Values ≠ desires (though can interact).

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: ACTION-003
Work: Unknown
Title: Free Acts as Value-Driven

Position:
Free acts driven by values, NOT by second-order desires (contra Frankfurt). Second-order desires can be warped.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: ACTION-004
Work: Unknown
Title: Rational vs. Intelligent Distinction

Position:
Rational = embodies due regard for interests. Intelligent = computational power. Irrational acts can be highly intelligent.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: ACTION-005
Work: Unknown
Title: Frankfurt's Analysis Insufficient

Position:
Frankfurt right about higher-order states but wrong that second-order desires sufficient. Rationalization problem. **EPISTEMOLOGY (9 positions): EP-004 to EP-014**

================================================================================
DOMAIN: AE (19 positions)
================================================================================

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: AE-018
Work: Unknown
Title: Drama Ages Better Than Comedy Due to Archetypal vs. Cultural Content

Position:
Drama endures because rooted in existential constants (death, love, guilt, betrayal) not cultural taboos. Comedy decays because depends on shared repressions that fade.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: AE-019
Work: Unknown
Title: Freud's Theory Explains Why Old Comedies Suck

Position:
Freud's theory: humor releases repressed psychic energy. Comedy ages poorly because depends on shared repressions/taboos - once taboos fade, jokes fall flat.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: AE-020
Work: Unknown
Title: M*A*S*H as Comfort Food for the Quietly Obedient

Position:
M*A*S*H fans love Hawkeye because they ARE Frank Burns but don't want to admit it. Show offers false rebellion - lets safe people pretend they're brave without risk.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: AE-021
Work: Unknown
Title: The Thin Blue Line / Errol Morris as Boring Stylistic Void

Position:
Errol Morris films boring - style over substance, manipulation over insight. Inflates content with cinematic gimmicks. Remembered for consequences not as compelling cinema.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: AE-022
Work: Unknown
Title: Apocalypse Now as Bloated Incoherent Spectacle

Position:
Apocalypse Now is bloated, incoherent spectacle - self-conscious attempt to create Great Work without discipline. Says nothing real about Vietnam, war, or human nature.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: AE-023
Work: Unknown
Title: In Cold Blood / Wilderness of Error / Apocalypse Now as Dishonest Works

Position:
These three works united by deeper commonality: fundamentally dishonest - betray realities they claim to explore, sacrifice truth for self-indulgence.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: AE-024
Work: Unknown
Title: Capote Withered After In Cold Blood Due to Unlivable Fantasy

Position:
Capote withered after In Cold Blood because he encountered embodiment of his unlivable sexual/emotional fantasy in Perry Smith. When fantasy collapsed, left with permanent starvation.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: AE-025
Work: Unknown
Title: Dr. Melfi / A.J. Soprano as Failed Characters

Position:
Dr. Melfi worst recurring character - stiff, judgmental, tone-deaf. Lorraine Bracco performing competence not inhabiting complexity. A.J. equally bad - Robert Iler brought no emotion or presence.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: AE-026
Work: Unknown
Title: ASMR as Soft-Core Porn Disguised as Therapy

Position:
ASMR is scam - soft-core pornography disguised as therapy. Relies on calculated cultural dishonesty. Most content features women making erotic mouth sounds while claiming therapeutic benefit.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: AE-027
Work: Unknown
Title: Husserl as Schizophrenic Drivel

Position:
Husserl's phenomenology not rigorous philosophical system but mind unraveling under guise of precision. Affective and cognitive structure bears disturbing resemblance to schizophrenia phenomenology. **EPISTEMOLOGY (1 positions): EP-115 to EP-115**

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: AE-028
Work: Unknown
Title: Star Wars as Jungian Dreamscape

Position:
Star Wars (1977) is not space opera but Jungian dreamscape - every frame steeped in archetype, guided by mythic structure, powered by psychological machinery Jung mapped. About soul, not space.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: AE-029
Work: Unknown
Title: Star Trek's Psychological Symmetry as Source of Durability

Position:
Star Trek's brilliance isn't stories but psychological symmetry: id pushes for passion, superego demands restraint, ego must choose/balance/synthesize/act. Each episode is microcosm of self in conflict.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: AE-030
Work: Unknown
Title: Satire Fails Without Systems Understanding

Position:
Literary satire falls apart if you don't understand the system you're mocking. Writers like Lewis portray middle-class work as absurd without understanding capital flows, risk underwriting, legal frameworks, infrastructure coordination.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: AE-031
Work: Unknown
Title: The Babbitt Problem: Mocking Components as Clowns

Position:
Babbitt may be windbag but he occupies place in real machinery of civilization - helps allocate space, facilitates growth, is node in economic network. Lewis doesn't see this because he never bothers. To him Babbitt is type not participant, clown not component.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: AE-032
Work: Unknown
Title: The Frank Burns Problem: Mocking the Machinery That Makes Everything Possible

Position:
Hawkeye mocks Frank Burns, but Burns follows procedure and keeps system running. Hawkeye mocks the machinery, but it's the machinery that makes surgery possible. Satire without respect equals superficiality.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: AE-033
Work: Unknown
Title: Snobbery as Epistemological Vice

Position:
Snobbery is not just social vice but epistemological one - a kind of built-in blindness. Lewis's portrayal of Babbitt suffers from defensiveness dressed up as superiority, presumption of guilt that ruins ability to see clearly.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: AE-034
Work: Unknown
Title: The Anthropologist Analogy for Bad Satire

Position:
Imagine anthropologist who despises tribe he's meant to observe - thinks rituals stupid, beliefs primitive. Maybe feels threatened by their strength, cohesion, joy, so adopts supercilious posture. How much will he learn? Nothing. His fieldwork is already over.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: AE-035
Work: Unknown
Title: Bach's Music as Engineering Not Just Expression

Position:
Bach's music isn't just expressive but engineered - in same sense as suspension bridge or cathedral. His fugues and chorales are systems: harmonic architectures, counterpunctual machines, vaults of sound built with structural intelligence and terrifying precision. This IS German engineering in musical form.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: AE-036
Work: Unknown
Title: Music as Intelligible Emotion - Soul Through System

Position:
Music at its best is intelligible emotion - emotion made knowable through form. What happens when human feeling is passed through filter of logic, structure, constraint and transformed into something enduring. Emotion is energy, structure is geometry, music is fusion. **EPISTEMOLOGY (9 positions): EP-151 to EP-159**

ID: EP-027

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-030
Work: Unknown
Title: A Priori Knowledge as Cognitive Framework (Not Framework Content)

Position:
A priori knowledge is not knowledge you have (content within framework) but knowledge you are (the framework itself). It is not the object of awareness but the subject that makes awareness possible.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-031
Work: Unknown
Title: Framework-Knowledge vs Content-Knowledge Distinction

Position:
Fundamental distinction between (1) structure-internal knowledge (learned, content) and (2) structure-constitutive knowledge (a priori, framework). All learned knowledge presupposes the framework.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-032
Work: Unknown
Title: Deep Unconsciousness of Cognitive Framework

Position:
Framework-constitutive structures are 'deeply unconscious' (Chomsky's term) - unlike Freudian unconscious. Cannot become conscious because consciousness presupposes them. **PHILOSOPHY OF LANGUAGE (1 positions): LANG-023 to LANG-023**

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-050
Work: Unknown
Title: AI Falsifies Enumerative Induction Model

Position:
AI systems demonstrate that successful induction does not proceed by enumerating instances and generalizing. Instead, AI uses pattern recognition, analogy, and constraint satisfaction that cannot be reduced to simple enumeration of cases.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-051
Work: Unknown
Title: Pattern Recognition as Alternative to Enumeration

Position:
Successful inductive reasoning operates through pattern recognition mechanisms that identify structural similarities rather than counting instances. AI systems reveal this by succeeding at induction without explicit enumeration.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-052
Work: Unknown
Title: AI Resolves Rationalism vs Empiricism Debate

Position:
AI systems demonstrate that knowledge acquisition requires both innate structure (rationalist element) and learning from data (empiricist element). Neither pure rationalism nor pure empiricism can account for AI's success. The debate is resolved by recognizing both are necessary.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-053
Work: Unknown
Title: Innate Architecture is Necessary for Learning

Position:
AI systems require substantial innate architectural constraints to learn successfully from data. This vindicates the rationalist insight that some knowledge structure must precede experience, while acknowledging the empiricist insight that specific content comes from experience.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-054
Work: Unknown
Title: Knowledge Acquisition is Neither Pure Discovery nor Pure Construction

Position:
AI reveals that knowledge acquisition is neither pure discovery of pre-existing facts (naive realism) nor pure construction from experience (radical constructivism). It involves interaction between innate processing architecture and environmental structure.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-055
Work: Unknown
Title: AI Solves the Gettier Problem

Position:
AI learning systems demonstrate a solution to the Gettier problem by showing that genuine knowledge requires not just justified true belief but also that the justification tracks truth through a reliable causal-computational process. AI systems that learn reliably exemplify this tracking relationship.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-056
Work: Unknown
Title: Reliable Process Theory of Knowledge via AI

Position:
AI systems reveal that knowledge requires beliefs formed through reliable processes that systematically track truth. This vindicates reliabilist theories of knowledge over traditional JTB (justified true belief) accounts.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-057
Work: Unknown
Title: Knowledge Systems Minimize Anomalies

Position:
Both human knowledge and AI systems operate by minimizing anomalies - discrepancies between expectations and observations. This convergence reveals anomaly minimization as a fundamental principle of rational cognition.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-058
Work: Unknown
Title: AI Learning Mirrors Scientific Theory Revision

Position:
The process by which AI systems update their models to accommodate new data mirrors the process of scientific theory revision in response to anomalies. This suggests a common underlying logic of belief revision.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-059
Work: Unknown
Title: Continuous Properties Are Cognitively Necessary

Position:
AI reveals that continuous (graded) properties are necessary for cognitive systems to handle uncertainty and partial information, but this doesn't entail that truth itself is non-binary. Epistemic gradations are compatible with metaphysical bivalence.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-060
Work: Unknown
Title: AI Vindicates Pragmatist Theory of Knowledge

Position:
AI development vindicates pragmatism's core insight that knowledge acquisition is fundamentally interactive rather than passive. AI systems learn through active engagement with their environment, validating pragmatist emphasis on the practical, interactive nature of inquiry.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-061
Work: Unknown
Title: AI as New Epistemic Faculty

Position:
Interaction with AI constitutes a genuinely new epistemic faculty - a fourth level of observation beyond passive observation, active interaction, and tool creation. AI enables rational interaction with our own capacity for rational interaction, generating unique knowledge.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-062
Work: Unknown
Title: Knowledge is Inherently Perspectival and Interactive

Position:
AI reveals that all knowledge, even 'objective' knowledge, begins from perspectival, interaction-based data driven by practical interests. There is no view from nowhere - even AI's knowledge is grounded in its interactions with reality.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-063
Work: Unknown
Title: Tool-Creating Interaction Generates Irreducible Knowledge

Position:
Creating tools (including AI) generates knowledge that cannot be obtained from merely using tools or observing passively. Each level of reflexive interaction (tool use, tool creation, AI development) reveals new knowledge irreducible to lower levels. **LOGIC (8 positions): LOGIC-016 to LOGIC-023**

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-064
Work: Unknown
Title: Two Kinds of Knowledge: Direct and Indirect

Position:
There are exactly two kinds of knowledge: direct (non-inferential, primitive) knowledge and indirect (inferential) knowledge. All knowledge falls into one of these two categories.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-065
Work: Unknown
Title: All Theoretical Knowledge is Inferential

Position:
All theoretical knowledge is inferential knowledge, though not all inferential knowledge is theoretical knowledge. Theoretical knowledge requires reasoning from observations to explanatory hypotheses.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-066
Work: Unknown
Title: Knowledge is Justified True Belief (But Not Vice Versa)

Position:
All knowledge is justified true belief, but not all justified true belief is knowledge. Additional conditions beyond justification, truth, and belief are required for knowledge.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-067
Work: Unknown
Title: Two Kinds of Dependence Relations: Causal and Logical

Position:
There are exactly two fundamental types of dependence relations: causal dependence relations and logical dependence relations. These are distinct and irreducible to each other.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-068
Work: Unknown
Title: Logical Dependence Relations Not Known Through Observation

Position:
Relations of logical dependence are not known through observation. They are known a priori, through conceptual analysis or reasoning, not through empirical investigation.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-069
Work: Unknown
Title: Causal Relations Known Through Observation

Position:
Causal relations are known through observation. Unlike logical relations, causal dependencies are empirical matters discoverable through perception and experience.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-070
Work: Unknown
Title: Analytic Knowledge is Always Knowledge of Dependence Relations

Position:
Analytic knowledge is always and necessarily knowledge of dependence-relations. To know analytic truths is to know how concepts or propositions depend on each other.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-071
Work: Unknown
Title: Propositions Are the Objects of Belief

Position:
Propositions, not objects or states of affairs, are the proper objects of belief. To believe is to take a proposition to be true.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-072
Work: Unknown
Title: Knowledge Distinct From Awareness

Position:
Knowledge must be sharply distinguished from mere awareness. One can be aware of something without knowing anything about it, and one can know things without being directly aware of them.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-073
Work: Unknown
Title: The Concept of Evidence: Causal Relatedness

Position:
One state of affairs e is evidence of another state of affairs e* if and only if e and e* are causally related such that knowledge of e's existence provides reason to believe in e*'s existence.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-074
Work: Unknown
Title: Information-Transmission as Structure-Preservation

Position:
Information-transmission is structure-preservation. An information-bearing series is one in which earlier events transmit their structure to later events through causal processes that preserve structural relationships.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-075
Work: Unknown
Title: Information Distinct From Evidence

Position:
All information is evidence, but not all evidence is information. Evidence requires only causal relatedness; information requires causal relatedness plus structure-preservation.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-076
Work: Unknown
Title: Information-Transmission as the Basis of Knowledge

Position:
Knowledge is based on information-transmission. Our sense-perceptions are isomorphs of the objects they represent, inheriting structure from their causes. Beliefs are knowledge only to the extent they are linked by information-transmissive series to corresponding realities.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-077
Work: Unknown
Title: Knowledge Independent of Statistical Reliability

Position:
The difference between knowledge and mere belief is not statistical. A belief is knowledge if and only if it is the end-result of an information-transmissive series, regardless of the general reliability of the mechanism that produced it.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-143
Work: Unknown
Title: The Frequency Theory of Probability is false

Position:
Frequency Theory (FT) - the view that probabilities are identical with statistical frequencies - is false. Refuted by W1/W2 thought experiment and smoking-cancer example. **LOGIC (7 positions): LOGIC-024 to LOGIC-030**

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-144
Work: Unknown
Title: Truth out of context as damaging as falsehood

Position:
Truths taken out of context, or made available to people who don't know how to contextualize them, can be as damaging as falsehoods and lead to confusion that enables acceptance of falsehoods.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: EP-145
Work: Unknown
Title: Plato's extreme rationalism is political, not epistemological

Position:
Plato's radical epistemological claim that observables are unreal 'shadows' while only pure thought accesses reality is not genuine epistemology but political belief presented as epistemological belief, driven by fear of political change.

Position:

Position:

Their political philosophies—which were very good—did engage the world; but to the extent that they did, they were almost anti-philosophical.

Work: Unknown

Empiricism collapses into the view that we can have knowledge of nothing except our own conscious states... So in their attempt to make philosophy engage the world, Locke and Hume empiricized philosophy. But in empiricizing philosophy, Locke and Hume made philosophy collapse into pure skepticism, pure skepticism being the most compete conceivable autistic withdrawal from reality.

Work: Unknown
Title: Conscious Experience as Epistemic Foundation

Work: Unknown

The subjective standpoint is not an epistemic limitation to be overcome but a constitutive feature of how conscious beings access reality. This means background beliefs that structure perception are part of the constitutive framework, not defeaters of justification.

ID: LANG-033
Work: Unknown
Title: AI Vindicates Semantics-Pragmatics Distinction

Position:
Large language models demonstrate a clear distinction between semantic content (literal meaning) and pragmatic interpretation (context-dependent meaning). The success of LLMs requires maintaining this distinction, vindicating classical theories of meaning against pragmatist attempts to collapse semantics into pragmatics.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: LANG-034
Work: Unknown
Title: Literal Meaning is Computationally Prior to Pragmatic Interpretation

Position:
AI systems must compute literal semantic content before applying pragmatic adjustments. This computational priority reveals that semantics is foundational and pragmatics is derivative, supporting classical over post-modern theories of meaning.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: LANG-035
Work: Unknown
Title: Context-Independence of Core Semantics

Position:
LLMs demonstrate that core semantic content can be represented context-independently and then applied across contexts. This vindicates the classical view that meaning has a stable core that pragmatic factors modulate rather than wholly constitute.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: LANG-036
Work: Unknown
Title: AI Vindicates Syntax-Semantics Interface

Position:
Large language models demonstrate that grammatical structure (syntax) and meaning (semantics) are distinct but systematically related. The success of LLMs requires explicit representation of this interface, vindicating classical grammatical theory against attempts to reduce one to the other.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: LANG-037
Work: Unknown
Title: Syntactic Structure Constrains Semantic Interpretation

Position:
AI language systems reveal that syntactic structure constrains possible semantic interpretations. This supports the classical view that grammar is not arbitrary convention but reflects systematic constraints on meaning composition.

ID: LANG-038
Work: Unknown
Title: Compositional Semantics Requires Syntactic Structure

Position:
The ability of LLMs to understand novel sentences demonstrates that semantic interpretation is compositional - the meaning of complex expressions derives systematically from their parts and syntactic structure. This requires and vindicates traditional compositional semantic theories.

Work: Unknown
Title: Grammar and Logic are Fundamentally Aligned

ID: LOGIC-011
Work: WORK-011
Title: Classical Logic as Formalization Not Discovery

Position:
Classical logic is fundamentally inadequate as a tool for reasoning because it requires more intelligence to recognize that an inference instantiates a logical law than to recognize the validity of the inference directly. Logic organizes existing knowledge about entailment but cannot generate new knowledge about entailment relationships.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: LOGIC-012
Work: WORK-011
Title: Performance vs. Competence-Demanding Inferences

Position:
Two fundamentally different types of inferential challenges exist: (1) Performance-demanding (straining computational/memory resources), (2) Competence-demanding (requiring genuine insight). Classical logic can only assist with the former.

ID: LOGIC-013
Work: WORK-011
Title: System L: AI-Based Discovery Logic

Position:
A radically different logical system exists in AI that actually helps reasoning through: (1) semantic networks representing concepts as relationship nodes, (2) meta-reasoning patterns generating new inferences, (3) defeasible reasoning allowing provisional inferences.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: LOGIC-014
Work: WORK-011
Title: Discovery-Justification Distinction in Logic

Position:
System L maintains crucial distinction between discovery procedures (can use any methods including inductive/analogical) and verification procedures (must employ deductive methods in deductive domains). Avoids psychologism while enabling reasoning assistance.

ID: LOGIC-023
Work: Unknown
Title: Grammatical Structure Guides Logical Inference

Position:
LLMs successfully perform logical reasoning by following grammatical structure, demonstrating that surface grammar encodes logical relationships. This vindicates the traditional view that grammatical form reveals logical form.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: LOGIC-024
Work: Unknown
Title: Entailment Defined as Logical Consequence

Position:
P entails Q if and only if Q is a logical consequence of P. If P entails Q and P is true, then Q must be true and may be legitimately inferred from P.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: LOGIC-025
Work: Unknown
Title: Confirmation Defined as Probability-Increase

Position:
P confirms Q if and only if P, supposing it true, increases the likelihood that Q is true. Confirmation does not by itself license inference from P to Q.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: LOGIC-026
Work: Unknown
Title: Conditions for Legitimate Inductive Inference

Position:
Q may legitimately be inferred from P if and only if: (a) the supposition that P is true and Q is false has fewer unexplainable consequences than the supposition that P and Q are both true, AND (b) the supposition that P is true has fewer unexplainable consequences than the supposition that P is false.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: LOGIC-027
Work: Unknown
Title: Four Principles: Entailment vs. Confirmation

Position:
Four logical principles hold: (i) Entailment is transitive; (ii) Confirmation is not transitive; (iii) Entailment is monotonic; (iv) Confirmation is non-monotonic. These differences show entailment and confirmation are fundamentally different relations.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: LOGIC-028
Work: Unknown
Title: Entailment Not Maximal Confirmation

Position:
Entailment is not maximal confirmation. Entailment is a logical notion concerning what is counterlogical; confirmation is an explanatory notion concerning what is counterexplanatory.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: LOGIC-029
Work: Unknown
Title: Confirmation-Relations Non-Objectual in Nature

Position:
Confirmation relations, though not themselves causal relations, sometimes hold in virtue of causal relations. But confirmation relates propositions, not objects or events.

ID: LOGIC-CP001
Work: Unknown
Title: Material Conditional Does Not Capture "If-Then" Meaning

Position:
The symbol "→" in classical logic (material conditional) does not mean "if...then" in natural language. It merely means "not both P and not-Q" and is strictly truth-conditional, lacking the modal/entailment force of natural language conditionals.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: LOGIC-CP002
Work: Unknown
Title: Natural Language Conditionals Are Modal

Position:
"If P, then Q" in natural language means "Q follows from P" or "not-Q is incompatible with P" - a modal notion involving possibility and impossibility, not reducible to truth-functional logic.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: LOGIC-CP003
Work: Unknown
Title: The Paradoxes of Material Implication Are Not Genuine Paradoxes

Position:
The so-called "paradoxes of validity" (e.g., that a false statement entails anything) are not real paradoxes but arise from misconstruing "P→Q" as meaning "if P, then Q" when it actually only means "not (P and not-Q)".

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: LOGIC-CP004
Work: Unknown
Title: Relevance Logic Misguided in Approach

Position:
Attempts by relevance logicians (Belnap, Anderson) to create truth-conditional approximations of natural language "if...then" are misconceived, as they try to model a fundamentally modal notion using truth-conditional methods.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: LOGIC-CP005
Work: Unknown
Title: Classical Logic Implicitly Requires Non-Truth-Conditional Conditionals

Position:
Classical logic is implicitly committed to a non-truth-conditional conception of conditionality, as the Law of Non-contradiction depends on the modal notion that no statement can be compatible with its own negation.

ID: META-CP001
Work: Unknown
Title: Moore's Proof of an External World Fails

Position:
G.E. Moore's famous proof of an external world (by holding up his hands) is unsuccessful and does not refute skepticism about the external world.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Work: Unknown
Title: There Is an External World

Position:
Despite problems with Moore's proof, we can establish that an external world exists.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Title: Descartes' Conception of Self Is Defensible

Position:

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: META-CP004
Work: Unknown
Title: Moore's Proof Begs the Question

Position:
G.E. Moore's attempt to prove an external world by holding up his hands begs the question against the skeptic because the skeptic would not grant the existence of hands as mind-independent objects.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: META-CP005
Work: Unknown
Title: Question-Begging Broader Than Premise-Conclusion Identity

Position:
An argument begs the question not only when the conclusion is identical to a premise, but when the premises would not be granted by one's opponent or when accepting the premises requires already accepting the conclusion.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: META-CP006
Work: Unknown
Title: Sophisticated Beliefs Are Distillations of Lower-Level Beliefs

Position:
Beliefs like "there exists an external world" are sophistications or distillations of lower-level beliefs like "there exists a hand here." The fact that children have the latter without the former doesn't show independent plausibility.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: META-CP007
Work: Unknown
Title: Non-Question-Begging Arguments Against Skepticism Possible

Position:
Unlike Moore's proof, some arguments against skepticism don't beg the question, such as arguing from the existence of mental states plus causation principles to the existence of external causes of those mental states.

ID: META-008
Work: Unknown
Title: Causality as Counterfactual Dependence

ID: META-003
Work: Unknown
Title: Anti-Constructivism

Position:
Constructivism self-refuting through reductio **PHILOSOPHY OF MIND (3 positions): MIND-002 to MIND-004**

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: META-011
Work: Unknown
Title: Binary Truth Despite Continuous Representation

Position:
AI systems demonstrate that truth remains fundamentally binary (true/false) even though cognitive systems represent information continuously. Continuous confidence values or fuzzy representations are epistemic features, not ontological features of truth itself. **METHODOLOGY (3 positions): METH-007 to METH-009**

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: META-012
Work: Unknown
Title: Causation as the Essence of Temporal Precedence

Position:
For one event e to precede another event e* is for there to be a possible causal process beginning with e and ending with e*. Simultaneity is the absence of such a process.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: META-013
Work: Unknown
Title: Continuity as the Essence of Causation

Position:
Effects are continuations of their causes. Causation essentially involves continuity - causal processes preserve structural relationships across temporal intervals without gaps.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: META-014
Work: Unknown
Title: Causation a Relation Between Events, Not Objects

Position:
Causation is fundamentally a relation between events, not between objects. Objects participate in causal relations only derivatively, in virtue of events involving those objects.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: META-015
Work: Unknown
Title: Conditions Identical with Event-Patterns

Position:
Conditions are identical with event-patterns. A condition is not a state but rather a pattern or type of event sequence that can be instantiated multiple times.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: META-016
Work: Unknown
Title: So-Called Changes Typically Identical with Meta-Changes

Position:
What are ordinarily called changes are typically meta-changes - changes in the rate, direction, or pattern of already-occurring changes rather than absolute transitions from rest to motion or vice versa.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: META-017
Work: Unknown
Title: Threshold Effects and Psychological Overdetermination

Position:
In psychology, causation often involves exceeding thresholds rather than simple sufficient conditions. An effect may require the confluence of multiple reasons, none sufficient alone but jointly sufficient once a threshold is exceeded.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: META-018
Work: Unknown
Title: Threshold Effects and the Analog-Digital Distinction

Position:
Discontinuous changes tend to involve threshold effects; continuous changes do not. To the extent the world changes discontinuously it has digital structure; to the extent continuously, analog structure.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: META-019
Work: Unknown
Title: Causes as INUS-Conditions

Position:
In most contexts, to say 'X caused Y' means 'X was an INUS condition for Y' - an Insufficient but Non-redundant part of an Unnecessary but Sufficient condition for Y's occurrence.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: META-020
Work: Unknown
Title: Counterfactuals Hold in Virtue of Dependence-Relations

Position:
All counterfactuals affirm the existence of instances of necessitation of some kind. Causal counterfactuals hold in virtue of causal dependence-relations; logical counterfactuals hold in virtue of logical dependence-relations.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: META-021
Work: Unknown
Title: David Lewis's Possible Worlds Analysis of Counterfactuals Rejected

Position:
David Lewis's analysis of counterfactuals in terms of similar possible worlds is false. Events have deep causal roots such that changing one event requires either massive world-differences or changes to deterministic mechanisms.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: META-022
Work: Unknown
Title: Program-Causality Distinguished from Token-Causality

Position:
Program-causality differs from token-causality. Sometimes the appropriate causal explanation cites a condition that guaranteed occurrence of token-causes rather than the token-causes themselves.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: META-023
Work: Unknown
Title: Causal Redundancy Defeats Counterfactual Analysis

Position:
Where there is causal redundancy, causal truths cannot be converted into counterfactual truths. 'X caused Y' can be true even when 'if X hadn't occurred, Y wouldn't have occurred' is false. **METHODOLOGY (9 positions): METH-010 to METH-018**
